<span id="freeTextContainer15101477970329389607">I was fooled by the exciting premise and pretty cover. Don't make the same mistake! Save yourselves!<br/><br/>I will try to summarize all the things I hated about <i>Abandon</i>.<br/><br/><b>The protagonist, Pierce</b>, was truly the most awful thing about the book. She was such an idiot it caused me physical pain. Sometimes I'd read something so pricelessly terrible that I just HAD to mark the page. This happened a grand total of SEVENTEEN TIMES. She was so. Freaking. Awful. Some highlights:<br/><br/><i>He still seemed pretty mad. A good si</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15101477970329389607" style="display:none">I was fooled by the exciting premise and pretty cover. Don't make the same mistake! Save yourselves!<br /><br />I will try to summarize all the things I hated about <i>Abandon</i>.<br /><br /><b>The protagonist, Pierce</b>, was truly the most awful thing about the book. She was such an idiot it caused me physical pain. Sometimes I'd read something so pricelessly terrible that I just HAD to mark the page. This happened a grand total of SEVENTEEN TIMES. She was so. Freaking. Awful. Some highlights:<br /><br /><i>He still seemed pretty mad. A good sign of this was when his chest started to rise and fall as if he'd been running, which it was doing now.</i><br /><br />So... you can tell he is mad because he's <i>breathing</i>?? That's funny, because I can tell Pierce is being an idiot whenever <i>she</i> breathes. At least she's consistent!<br /><br />Oh, and she has taken the written portion of the driver's test 42 times. And failed each time. If you had any lingering doubts about how stupid she is, do you feel them fading away right about now?<br /><br />But here's the pinnacle of her wondrous awfulness:<br /><br /><i>Sure, I'd been kicked out of school. I couldn't seem to go more than an hour without craving a caffeinated beverage. And a guy I'd met while I was dead had popped by unexpectedly and caused me to be slapped with a seven-figure civil suit.<br /><br />But I was feeling positive about the future.</i><br /><br />That's great, Pierce! That is just so great that your daddy has to pay more than a million dollars for your BS. Seriously, your optimism is so endearing and just <b>so freaking great</b>. <br /><br />I HATE HER.<br /><br /><b>Also, Meg Cabot's writing is terrible.</b> The book didn't even make sense. When John, the <i>lurrvee</i> interest, is taken aback and surprised, his voice is described as being like thunder. I'm sorry, but wouldn't that be more appropriate for when he is ANGRY?<br /><br />Oh whoops, I forgot. When he's angry, his chest rises and falls. How silly of me.<br /><br />None of Pierce's thoughts make sense in response to what's happening. I couldn't even file that under Pierce's craposity, it was all Cabot's laziness. And what was with the weird, annoying repititions? Some chick had a tattoo that said "Check yourself before you wreck yourself" and Cabot, for some unfathomable reason, felt the need to toss that line in every couple pages. As its own paragraph, in italics, as if she had just said something very, very deep. It hardly ever made any sense in the context it was used, either.<br /><br />The pacing was bad, too. She threw us into the story way late in the timeline, then tried to give tiny flashbacks to intrigue me about what had gone on before. It didn't work, I was not intrigued. I was confused and freaking bored. <br /><br />Pretty much the only thing I enjoyed was the presence of Pierce's Uncle Chris and cousin Alex. If Pierce had just stayed dead the first time and the whole book had been about the life and times of her extended family, that would have been a decent book. Except for the fact that Cabot has a habit of destroying her protagonsists, so never mind, Alex would probably be a whiny child in that alternate book.<br /><br />I probably don't even have to say this, but it's clear I will never be reading Cabot again*. She hurts me deep inside.<br /><br /><br />*as soon as I finish the Princess Diaries series. Then I'll be done, I swear**.<br /><br />** okay fine, and probably this series too. I have an obsessive-compulsive need to finish everything I start.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15101477970329389607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_157794596" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157794596" />
    <a title="Auntb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4351750-auntb"><img alt="Auntb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307504420p2/4351750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157794596?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Auntb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Auntb" href="/user/show/4351750-auntb">Auntb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157794596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13262983431770962973">Abandon by Meg Cabot.<br/>Reviewed at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://ya-sisterhood.blogspot.com/2011/03/abandon-by-meg-cabot.html'>http://ya-sisterhood.blogspot.com/201...</a><br/>Reviewed by: Baby Sister Brittany<br/>Release Date: April 26th, 2011 (Get your Pre-Order on, kids)<br/>The Sisters say: Spooky, Swoon-worthy, and Scintillating<br/>EDIT: Currently giving away an ARC on the blog. Contest ends 4.13.11<br/><br/><br/><br/>Abandon all hope ye who enter here?<br/><br/> Try abandon those attempts at sleep and read this book in one sitting!<br/><br/>It’s hard to remember the first Young Adult book I read that captured me all those years ago, but I do </span>
  <span id="freeText13262983431770962973" style="display:none">Abandon by Meg Cabot.<br />Reviewed at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://ya-sisterhood.blogspot.com/2011/03/abandon-by-meg-cabot.html">http://ya-sisterhood.blogspot.com/201...</a><br />Reviewed by: Baby Sister Brittany<br />Release Date: April 26th, 2011 (Get your Pre-Order on, kids)<br />The Sisters say: Spooky, Swoon-worthy, and Scintillating<br />EDIT: Currently giving away an ARC on the blog. Contest ends 4.13.11<br /><br /><br /><br />Abandon all hope ye who enter here?<br /><br /> Try abandon those attempts at sleep and read this book in one sitting!<br /><br />It’s hard to remember the first Young Adult book I read that captured me all those years ago, but I do remember the first YA paranormal romance I ever read, and that was The Mediator series by Meg Cabot. If you have a thing for ghosts, especially swoon-worthy Spanish ones, you should check it out. I feel a little bit as if Meg Cabot has come full circle with her latest book. The Mediator featured ghosts stuck in the world of the living, while Abandon features a young girl, who faces the prospect of being stuck in the Underworld.<br /><br />Pierce’s story is told in pieces throughout the book with the past and present interwoven, but this much you glean early on—Pierce died, and in the Underworld she attracts the attention of John—the keeper of the Underworld. He’s not quite Hades, but rather has inherited this job. Pierce was determined to get back to her old life, and she succeeds, but John has to pay the price.<br /><br />Things I loved about the book:<br />1. Once again… Greek Mythology. In case you can’t tell—we love the Greeks here at YA Sisterhood! When I heard that this book was a re-telling of the Persephone myth, I was a bit reluctant to dive right into it honestly. I’d just read the Goddess Test (See our previous review) and I wasn’t sure that I wanted to read two books with the same plot within a two-week period. But they couldn’t be more different! I would say Abandon is only loosely inspired by the Persephone myth. This story is entirely it’s own.<br /><br />2. John. I liked scary, keeper of the underworld John. I liked sweet “I talk to children” John. I liked strong, dangerous “I ride a giant horse, don’t mess with me” John. And I LOVED “I suffer endlessly because of you, but I don’t care” John. I just loved John. John. John. John. (I’m hoping he’ll be like Beetlejuice and suddenly appear when I say his name three times). John really made this book for me. Pierce was an interesting narrator, and I enjoyed her story, but John had all my attention. He is at once profoundly human and utterly inhuman. He gets the worst of both worlds. He experiences all the pain and suffering of the human world (more so, in fact), but has the detached, hardened emotions of someone who controls where you go in the afterlife. And he has the immortality of the gods, which only gives him longer to stew in his loneliness. I can’t wait for the next book to learn more about him—how he became the keeper of the Underworld and what he had to go through after Pierce left.<br /><br /><br />3. The setting in the Florida Keys. When I think Florida Keys—I think sunshine and summer and bikinis and fun. This book had all of that, but it also had a layer of darkness and danger. The setting was lush and decadent and fascinating. I never for a moment thought—why would the Florida Keys have anything to do with the Underworld? It all just clicks into place perfectly!<br /><br />4. The twists! Oh, the twists!!! I can’t tell you much more except that it’s pretty… twisted. J<br /><br />I’ve seen some people complain that the book takes too long to get going. And it’s true, that you don’t really get the full story of what exactly happened to Pierce until fairly late in the book, but I actually liked the mystery. It was like puzzle—Meg Cabot gives you these little patchwork pieces, and the intensity only builds as the pieces start to fall into place.<br /><br />I, for one, am ecstatic with Meg Cabot’s return to the Paranormal world. Count me in for the adventure! Add this to your to-read pile (and while you’re at it, throw The Mediator series on there too). </span>
  <a data-text-id="13262983431770962973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103191235" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103191235" />
    <a title="Crystal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250501-crystal"><img alt="Crystal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378941415p2/2250501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103191235?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal" href="/user/show/2250501-crystal">Crystal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250501-crystal?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103191235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1618539888696366434">Pierce died. She died and discovered that bright lights are not the only thing a person can encounter after they take their last breath. The thing though is that Pierce grabs her own second chance and when she wakes up she learns that not everything was a dream and that John is indeed real. Sounds intriguing right? Well I bought into it and I am sad to say that my description, as plain and short as it is, in my opinion is way more interesting than most of this book. I am really interested in Gre</span>
  <span id="freeText1618539888696366434" style="display:none">Pierce died. She died and discovered that bright lights are not the only thing a person can encounter after they take their last breath. The thing though is that Pierce grabs her own second chance and when she wakes up she learns that not everything was a dream and that John is indeed real. Sounds intriguing right? Well I bought into it and I am sad to say that my description, as plain and short as it is, in my opinion is way more interesting than most of this book. I am really interested in Greek mythology so when I find a book, which seem to be more and more these days, I want to devour it and see what new spins and fun I can read about. I am so disappointed in this one because I can really see a great story in there somewhere, Ms.Cabot just fills the book with so many boring and mundane subplots that the real story gets left behind.<br />There were so many things that bothered me throughout this book. The first being the whole love fest. I know YA is known for its love at first sight and usually I can buy into it, but Pierce and John have very limited contact. I mean, at least my understanding, is that they have only had maybe 4 encounters and in all of them Pierce is the damsel in distress and John has to save the day then flee. So, I do not buy that they love each other, hell I don't even buy that they are lusting after each other.<br />Another pet peeve is that everything wrapped up way too quickly and Pierce figured the main plot out with no real evidence. It felt like the story was getting too long and the author decided to let Pierce in on her secret without having to work for it. Then the solution was just so simple I wanted to scream. I know that I am complaining that I didn't like the book and by my saying that it wasn't long enough seems weird but I wanted a real story. I devoted enough of my time that I felt like I deserved a true ending not a cop out.<br />The one person who I found interesting got very limited page time. I really want to know more about Richard and his life. He seems like a very interesting character and I hope that the author lets him pop up more in future installments, I might even read them if this happens.<br />Last thing the author had way too many subplots. I have so many questions! Why was Alex happy? Why did he detest the A-wings? What happened with Uncle Chris? What is the whole Coffin Night thing and will the seniors get caught? I think I was more wrapped up in the high school drama than the actual Underworld plot.<br />So, I know that my review isn't great but I want to say that I think Ms.Cabot has a great idea and I really hope that she fine tunes some things and makes the sequel tighter than its predecessor. I think if you are a fan of Meg Cabot then you might want to try this one just know that screaming at Pierce is acceptable. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1618539888696366434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_158822788" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158822788" />
    <a title="S.A. Larsen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3601031-s-a-larsen"><img alt="S.A. Larsen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444071519p2/3601031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158822788?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.A. Larsen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.A. Larsen" href="/user/show/3601031-s-a-larsen">S.A. Larsen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to S.A. by: </span>
      ARC provided by publisher
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158822788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9267723305337768994">~ A timeless Greek myth brought to modern times with a unique slant that titillates the heart. Cabot has masterfully cast Death as one of many (thought of) death deities, who's been hardened by his circumstances. The reader slowly watches his heart open wide as he, like Hades, finds what he's lacking in a human girl. And in this case, she's just a little tweaked-side of normal. ~<br/><br/>On the outside, the story itself has typical teen nuances as well as struggles: the girl who doesn't quite fit it, a f</span>
  <span id="freeText9267723305337768994" style="display:none">~ A timeless Greek myth brought to modern times with a unique slant that titillates the heart. Cabot has masterfully cast Death as one of many (thought of) death deities, who's been hardened by his circumstances. The reader slowly watches his heart open wide as he, like Hades, finds what he's lacking in a human girl. And in this case, she's just a little tweaked-side of normal. ~<br /><br />On the outside, the story itself has typical teen nuances as well as struggles: the girl who doesn't quite fit it, a family that is all but normal, a move of location, and a secret--the girl has a near-death experience only she's not just near Death; she chats with Him. What's even more unique is that Death is a main character--and he's hot. Eventually, the reader even discovers that he's sensitive and has a conscious. <br /><br />There's a bit of a historical twist threaded within the plot, giving it depth and a natural verve. The story simply isn't a modern remake of Hades (the reigning king of the underworld) and Persephone (his love interest). It's so much more.<br /><br />Cabot does a wonderful job of taking that story from Greek mythology and implanting it in today's teen society. The MC, Pierce, is authentic, as she's not only trying to normal--with a death deity longing for your loins, that's not all that easy--but fit into a new school with the typical high school cliques and head games.<br /><br />The initial element I always notices about a book is its cover. The first words are so important in a story, but in reality the initial impression is in the dressing--the cover. Abandon's artwork is beautiful, simple, and elegant. I usually make a mental note of the cover while I'm reading, trying to find the relation between the coating of the book and the story itself. And within this cover...here lies a message.<br /><br />After I'd finished reading, I realized that the title does have a more symbolic meaning them anything else. Many people have felt Abandoned in some form or another and at some point in their life. Many of Cabot's characters in ABANDON have experienced the lost of being abandoned or at least the feeling of such emotion.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to any paranormal and/or romance enthusiast, as well as those interested in Greek mythology. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9267723305337768994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_166007545" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166007545" />
    <a title="Milly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4000502-milly"><img alt="Milly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291008553p2/4000502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166007545?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milly" href="/user/show/4000502-milly">Milly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166007545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3889046740275872123">So this is supposed to be a retelling of the Greek mythology story of Hades and Persephone. I honestly don't know much about their story aside from what I read in Rick Riordan's Percy Jackson and the Lightning Thief. But since I'm not well versed on this mythological story, I am unable to make accurate comparisons between the two. And I think being unfamiliar with this story actually helped this book for me because I found Abandon's plot refreshing and intriguing as I haven't read any books usin</span>
  <span id="freeText3889046740275872123" style="display:none">So this is supposed to be a retelling of the Greek mythology story of Hades and Persephone. I honestly don't know much about their story aside from what I read in Rick Riordan's Percy Jackson and the Lightning Thief. But since I'm not well versed on this mythological story, I am unable to make accurate comparisons between the two. And I think being unfamiliar with this story actually helped this book for me because I found Abandon's plot refreshing and intriguing as I haven't read any books using this same plot.<br /><br />The main protagonist of Abandon is Pierce Oliviera, a 17-year old girl who recently had a near death experience and in the process met John, who happened to be the ruler of the Underworld, while waiting for the boat that was to take her to heaven. Somehow John was able to trick Pierce to go with him to the Underworld but when Pierce realizes her mistake, she smartly escapes John and the Underworld, as well as escape death and returns back to life after being injected adrenaline straight to her heart. When Pierce wakes up from all of these, she's unsure whether John was for real or if she just dreamed it all until she realizes that the necklace John gave her while she was in the Underworld with him was still hanging around her necklace. <br /><br />The necklace. According to John, the necklace is supposed to protect Pierce from evil. Apparently, this necklace was rich in history and was once owned by Marie Antoinette but was considered t o have brought bad luck to the bearer or wearer of it. As for Pierce, it appeared to have brought trouble for her as well but John always manages to find her and save her from the danger that awaited her. <br /><br />Pierce. She's an only child and used to an affluent lifestyle but is unpretentious and very caring of other people's well-being. She almost died trying to save an injured bird and caught John's attention when she came to him worried that his horse almost trampled him. Pierce appears to find and attract trouble and we later find out why this is. Aside from being pretty and having ADD, Pierce doesn’t really stand out as a protagonist for me. She doesn’t seem to have the drive or knows what she wants to do with her life. I don’t know if this is because of her near death experience but I would think coming out of such a monumental experience would drive you to want to live your life and not just cruise along. Her character is much too two-dimensional.<br /> <br />John. John’s character is more intriguing and is more colorful. His story makes Abandon. There’s more to him that meets the eye. Pierce first meets John as a teenager when she was seven years old at the Isla Huesos Cemetery during her grandfather's funeral. John Hayden is now the ruler of the Underworld and is smitten with Pierce after meeting her for the second time, entranced by Pierce's pretty eyes and her big heart. John is described as this very tall, dark, and handsome teenager, dressed in black and leaves a trail of scarlet blossoms in his wake. There's something dark and scary about him but at the same time sexy and fascinating. Though he doesn't quite know how to express his feelings to Pierce, his constant presence when she's in danger is endearing to her and Pierce can't seem to stay away from him either even after she finds out that he's from the Underworld. And being with him could mean her staying in the Underworld for eternity. Yes, she’s afraid of him for obvious reasons but she still can’t deny him. <br /><br />Despite the back and forth of present and past experiences of Pierce to build the story, I found this book a quick read. This book pretty much serves as the building block to the Abandon trilogy. I thought it was very clever of Cabot to tie up the history of Key West to John’s story and make Key West as the entrance to the Underworld. I didn’t go as far to research the truth about the skeletons of the dead surfacing on the ground after hurricanes and the reason why the dead in Key West are placed in crypts but my interest was definitely peaked. And what of the Coffin Night? How true was this as well? Cabot has certainly infused some interesting tidbits and plots into the story. It’s enough to keep me reading and waiting for the sequel to know more about John’s life and how he became the ruler of the Underworld, how to defeat the Furies, and what becomes of their pairing. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3889046740275872123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It's not like the cover is enticing, so honestly, <i>why</i>?<br/><br/>Answer: Because the cover of the third book caught my eye, and when I realised it was a whole new series I hadn't read already, I got super excited, and checked out the first one.<br/><br/>The main character, the protagonist, is super shallow, super whiny, and very frustrating. Worse narrators have not </span>
  <span id="freeText7558155591672725487" style="display:none">I think the library I'm a member of specialises in stocking books like this one. Books which make me go:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489860543ra/22257717.gif" alt="Uggh" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>For starters, why did I even pick up the book? It's not like the cover is enticing, so honestly, <i>why</i>?<br><br>Answer: Because the cover of the third book caught my eye, and when I realised it was a whole new series I hadn't read already, I got super excited, and checked out the first one.<br><br>The main character, the protagonist, is super shallow, super whiny, and very frustrating. Worse narrators have not existed. (I'm not kidding, <b>she makes Bella Swan appear interesting</b>.)<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489861506ra/22257851.gif" alt="Bella says thanks" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>She loves referencing to things that have happened in her past, but she never really gets to the point. She is petty, selfish, and unrealistic, but that's apparently okay, because she has neurological issues. <b>
  <i>This entire book makes light of people who actually have real psychological issues.</i>
</b><br><br>And getting her dad slapped with a seven figure lawsuit because she's a spoilt brat is apparently all right, because he's a multi-billionaire, and that excuses how she has little value for money. Or let me be more specific. She openly states multiple times that her dad throws money around, but she's not the same, because according to her <i>boooooyfriend</i> she always cares for the people and living beings around her.<br><br>Do I spy a Mary Sue?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489861506ra/22257852.gif" alt="Yup" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let's talk about that <s>boy</s> <s>man</s> male thing, shall we? His name is John, and he exists only to tell Pierce how perfect, innocent, and pretty she is. Yet, he's also mercurial enough to yell at her tons. He has a disposition towards being violent, but that's okay, because <i>he's just sad</i>! And also, he gave her this huuuuuge diamond to protect her from evil, so wow, he's awesome, and no matter what an asshole he is, <i>Pierce will just forgive him</i>. <br><br>[IMO, he’s abusive, and that’s romanticised.]<br><br>And in the end, Pierce agrees to stay with John, in his underworld whatever (despite his bringing her there without heeding her protests), because he tells her he loves her. <i>They've met only <u>seven</u> fucking times, including the last time where he tells her he loves her.</i> Here’s a quick summary of how their seven(!) meetings go:<br><br>—The first time John saw Pierce, she's seven and John's immortal and has been around forever. (I'll let that speak for itself.) <br>—The second time, he tries to hold her hostage. <br>—The third and fourth times, he almost kills people. <br>—The fifth time, he yells at her, throws a tantrum, and vandalises property. <br>—The sixth time, he lures her out of her house under false pretenses and kisses her when she tries to leave. <br>—The seventh time, he low-key abducts her.<br><br><i>But all that's okay, because he <b>wuvs</b> her!</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489862252ra/22257898.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(I never thought I'd find Trump useful in any form, haha.)<br><br>This book gets a one star rating, because Goodreads doesn't have negative ratings. <i>Sigh.</i><br><br>[Update: Subsequent to reading this book, I’ve come across worse books. So if <i>those</i> are one star reads, then this has to be two.]<br><br>Will I be reading the sequel?<br><br>You know the answer.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489862252ra/22257897.gif" alt="No." class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_161445394" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161445394" />
    <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales"><img alt="Dark Faerie Tales" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253675501p2/2766672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161445394?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dark Faerie Tales" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales">Dark Faerie Tales</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2766672-dark-faerie-tales?shelf=reviewed-by-angela">reviewed-by-angela</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161445394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8727343539469053753">Quick & Dirty: Unfortunately, Abandon starts out slow and continues to drag. The narrative is stilted and confusing, and the character development is minimal. Many elements of the story fail to satisfy.<br/><br/>Opening Sentence: Anything can happen in the blink of an eye.<br/><br/>The Review:<br/><br/>Pierce Oliviera had a near death experience. Her parent’s relationship completely fell apart and her life is in utter turmoil. She moves to Isla Huesos, the Island of Bones, with her mother. Pierce’s near death experience is p</span>
  <span id="freeText8727343539469053753" style="display:none">Quick &amp; Dirty: Unfortunately, Abandon starts out slow and continues to drag. The narrative is stilted and confusing, and the character development is minimal. Many elements of the story fail to satisfy.<br /><br />Opening Sentence: Anything can happen in the blink of an eye.<br /><br />The Review:<br /><br />Pierce Oliviera had a near death experience. Her parent’s relationship completely fell apart and her life is in utter turmoil. She moves to Isla Huesos, the Island of Bones, with her mother. Pierce’s near death experience is pretty strange, even for a near death experience. John Hayden, her Underworld captor, tells her that she must remain with him. Even though Pierce was able to escape the Underworld, she can’t seem to get rid of John Hayden, who wants to take her back to the Underworld. Pierce struggles with her new surroundings, attending a new school and making new friends, all the while wondering why she’s so important to John Hayden.<br /><br />Abandon is the first book in a new trilogy based on the Hades and Persephone myth. Unfortunately, Abandon isn’t the dark reimagining that I expected. I love Greek Mythology, so I had high expectations. Abandon has an interesting premise, but the story never lives up to its potential. It’s repetitive, slow, and somewhat uneven in developing its characters’ motivations.<br /><br />Pierce Oliviera, our narrator, doesn’t tell a compelling story. The narrative voice is confusing, distracting, and many of the characters fail to make you care about them. I think the story suffers largely because of its structure and its execution fails to deliver. The story is told out of sequence, alternating between past and present events. The bevy of flashbacks are hard to follow. You never get a sense that you have a grasp on the timeline of events or their importance. The flashbacks never seem to have a real ending or resolution, yet they move onto the next bit of sparse details. Pierce isn’t a particularly bright, likable, resourceful or practical heroine. She was always a day late and a dollar short in arriving to the correct conclusions.<br /><br />Abandon also lacks real action. I found myself wondering when something truly exciting or relevant was going to happen. I was hoping for anything to move the plot forward, anything to keep the reader engaged. The worldbuilding and mythology never quite gets off the ground. There isn’t any real connection or romance between Pierce and John. He has very little real presence in this book and what little exposure he did get in the book didn’t leave a lasting impression. John feels somewhat tacked on and underdeveloped.<br /><br />Overall, Abandon isn’t a dark journey into or out of the Underworld. Some readers might have a hard time establishing a connection with the characters, and this story is all build-up with no pay-off. Many important plot elements are simply revealed too late to be effective. As far as retellings go, Abandon departs so much from its source material that it ends up having little to do with the Hades and Persephone myth, leaving the reader feeling abandoned.<br /><br />Notable Scene:<br /><br />All I said was “Hey” in an attempt to get the rider’s attention…just as he was shouting at everyone in the other line to stay where they were — an order they seemed cowed by the harshness of his tone into obeying.<br /><br />I had no idea such a brutal tone could come from the sweet man I remembered — the one who’d made a bird come back alive — from my grandfather’s funeral. I stood there paralyzed with fright…<br /><br />…until the next thing I knew, charcoal black hooves were slashing the air just inches from my head as the horse reared, snorting in outrage.<br /><br />Then I ducked, afraid for my life, throwing my hands over my face to protect my eyes. A second later, those enormous hooves came exploding down again, spraying bits of sand everywhere, and I was diving for safety.<br /><br />That’s when a noise like the loudest thunderclap I’d ever heard filled the cavern. I wasn’t sure if it was a real thunderclap or the sound of the horse’s body as it crashed onto the beach, one of its back legs having slipped in the sand beneath it.<br /><br />A male voice shouted something. When I looked up from where I’d crouched in an effort not to be killed, I realized the shout came from the rider. He’d cried out the horse’s name — Alastor, as near as I could tell — and was kicking his boots from the stirrups as the horse scrambled back to its feet.<br /><br />It was only then that I realized — with a physical shock that jolted me nearly as much as the horse’s violent reaction had — that this was no nightmare. If it had been, I’d have woken by now. I wouldn’t be tasting sand in my mouth.<br /><br />And the man I’d met the day of my grandfather’s funeral wouldn’t have suddenly been standing over me, staring down at me with silver eyes that held not the slightest hint of recognition…or humanity.<br /><br />The Abandon Trilogy:<br /><br />1. Abandon<br /><br />2. Underworld<br /><br />FTC Advisory: Scholastic provided me with a copy of Abandon. No goody bags, sponsorships, “material connections,” or bribes were exchanged for my review. In addition, I don’t receive affiliate fees for anything purchased via links from my site.</span>

    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161777657?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780545387699" href="/book/show/11103922-abandon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161777657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11453602831628644549">Apparently, unbeknownst to me, this was a retelling of the story of Persephone, but I won't be able to really compare or critique on that point because I haven't read the classic story (I know I'm lame); I only know the very basic -queen of the underworld- myth and as I read a few of the reviews I've noticed those who have read the classic tale don't like it as much. Nevertheless, I thought it was fresh and original - a fun read with a hint of mystery and a few twists.<br/><br/>This is going to be a trilo</span>
  <span id="freeText11453602831628644549" style="display:none">Apparently, unbeknownst to me, this was a retelling of the story of Persephone, but I won't be able to really compare or critique on that point because I haven't read the classic story (I know I'm lame); I only know the very basic -queen of the underworld- myth and as I read a few of the reviews I've noticed those who have read the classic tale don't like it as much. Nevertheless, I thought it was fresh and original - a fun read with a hint of mystery and a few twists.<br /><br />This is going to be a trilogy so the first book is mostly the setup to initiate us to her world and characters. It wasn't full of fluff, though. There is definite plot and interesting story line developments. Of course, there is also Greek mythology involved which is interesting in of itself.<br /><br />Let's start with the characters. The protagonist, Pierce, is a bit skittish, but likable nonetheless. I could easily relate to her and understand her emotions. The secondary characters weren't especially developed but due to the advancement of the story, I imagine we will get to know them more in the following books. This one was primarily about Pierce and her relationship with John - which is very love/hate. John is… I haven't quite figured him out really. He's like a charming jerk - but that may simply be perception since his motives weren't all disclosed. So we'll see where it goes.<br /><br />The writing was good. We're told Pierce's story with the past and present interwoven. So we get snippets of what happened in the past that helps keep the story intriguing and mysterious. It does take a while to get all the pieces into place, but I liked the slow pace. The author took time to build up the intensity and details in the story; It was never boring. The ending though seemed a bit abrupt; just when things started to get real interesting, it ends. But I will forgive this since it's the first in a trilogy, so it's obviously not really over.<br /><br />Oh… and what's with all these men wearing tasseled shoes? Ick!<br /><br />As a solitary book, since nothing much happened I would have felt underwhelmed, but I know it's only the beginning of a story and I still found the plot and characters very intriguing. It kept my interest and I really hope the sequel won't disappoint.</span>

<div id="review_163932546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163932546" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4387706-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568309174p2/4387706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163932546?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/4387706-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163932546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9981056676740352240"> Meg Cabot's Abandon was a gripping dark tale that had me at page one. As YA PNR Fictional Mythology is becoming more and more popular, it's becoming increasingly difficult to maintain originality. Being a lover of mythology, I am overjoyed with books that are imaginative and creative yet still stick to the original concept. Abandon was one of those books.<br/> <br/>Abandon is not only extraordinary but extremely entertaining with a creative twist intertwining modern day times with age old mythology but t</span>
  <span id="freeText9981056676740352240" style="display:none"> Meg Cabot's Abandon was a gripping dark tale that had me at page one. As YA PNR Fictional Mythology is becoming more and more popular, it's becoming increasingly difficult to maintain originality. Being a lover of mythology, I am overjoyed with books that are imaginative and creative yet still stick to the original concept. Abandon was one of those books.<br /> <br />Abandon is not only extraordinary but extremely entertaining with a creative twist intertwining modern day times with age old mythology but the thrills, chills and suspense factor is what kept me reading well into the night. There wasn’t as much outward romance as I was expecting but the undercurrent was there and it was powerful! I’m so thankful this is a trilogy because I think Ms. Cabot has only scratched the surface of her incredibly imaginative and creative version of the Underworld mythology. Personally, I can’t wait to read more about John and Pierce but I am also interested in the secondary characters, which played a critical part in the book. A One-Sit-Read for this reviewer!<br /> <br />Abandon tells the tale of Pierce, a teenager who is incredibly empathetic and born to privilege. Life was good for Pierce until she died. Pierce escapes the keeper of the Underworld, John, in what I can only describe as a truly fantastical mythical way. Afterwards, Pierce seems to be troubled and from others perspectives, violent as opposed to seeing this as a second chance at life or a miracle, as most think she should feel. But, they don’t know the truth; they don’t know about John, keeper of the Underworld and apparently, keeper of Pierce. When violence occurs every time Pierce is threatened she is blamed for the violence that occurs until finally her mother takes her to a small island off the Florida Keys where she grew up and where her family still resides. It’s there that Pierce starts to get answers to questions, questions about things she didn’t even know existed until she moved there. Things that just may land her in the last place she wants to go back to: The Underworld.<br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9981056676740352240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_229119871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229119871" />
    <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine"><img alt="Mimi Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314137947p2/6110599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229119871?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Valentine" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine">Mimi Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=boys-i-wish-were-real">boys-i-wish-were-real</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229119871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14329360646535548771">Meg Cabot will always continue to be one of the wittiest authors on my watch, and that doesn't change with this sweet re-telling of the Hades and Persephone myth!<br/><br/>Although <b>Abandon</b> was a little slow to start, it was such an easy book to fly through in one sitting. I loved how you could never tell exactly where it was going. You just had to sit back and enjoy the ride, which was really refreshing! The only thing I found hard to swallow was how many flashbacks were incorporated in the story because </span>
  <span id="freeText14329360646535548771" style="display:none">Meg Cabot will always continue to be one of the wittiest authors on my watch, and that doesn't change with this sweet re-telling of the Hades and Persephone myth!<br /><br />Although <b>Abandon</b> was a little slow to start, it was such an easy book to fly through in one sitting. I loved how you could never tell exactly where it was going. You just had to sit back and enjoy the ride, which was really refreshing! The only thing I found hard to swallow was how many flashbacks were incorporated in the story because it slowed down the pace.<br /><br />Our heroine, Pierce, was such a kind, caring, and considerate girl, but I felt like she was made from a mold I'd seen so many times before: shy and a little too selfless. The story was very well-written but I never felt like Pierce's voice shone through and that made it really hard to connect with her. I wanted to see more of the strength that the author implied was there! <br /><br />But John — complete with his dark and broodiness that made him a totally swoon-worthy character — was the perfect love interest for Pierce! ♥ Their whole relationship was so incredibly sweet, and near the end, I found myself smiling at their interactions. This may have been a Hades/Persephone re-telling, but they put their own captivating spin on it.<br /><br />Thoughtful and sweet, <b>Abandon</b> may not have been a favourite, but it was a beautiful start to a bound-to-be enticing trilogy. You should definitely give it a shot! I'm really excited to see where Meg Cabot will take this story with the future installments! :)<br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> This was more of a borrow read for me, but if you're a Meg Cabot fan or a huge Greek mythology lover, then you might want to look into investing in this book!<br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.com/2012/03/review-abandon.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>)</span>

<div id="review_196385111" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Maria " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5769334-maria"><img alt="Maria " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600318539p2/5769334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196385111?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria " href="/user/show/5769334-maria">Maria </a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer196385111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9695741216572423999">We all wonder what it would be like in the afterlife.<br/>Will be taken to heaven, hell or will we remain in the in between.<br/>Pierce had a glimpse of what lies after we die.<br/><br/>Pierce died.<br/>She caught a glimpse of what it was like in the Underworld.<br/>She was supposed to stay there until she successfully escaped.<br/>She thought everything would be back to normal.<br/>But she was wrong.<br/>She hasn’t been normal since.<br/>Pierce and her mother moved to Isla Huesos where they thought they’d get a new start.<br/>But the more Pierce tr</span>
  <span id="freeText9695741216572423999" style="display:none">We all wonder what it would be like in the afterlife.<br />Will be taken to heaven, hell or will we remain in the in between.<br />Pierce had a glimpse of what lies after we die.<br /><br />Pierce died.<br />She caught a glimpse of what it was like in the Underworld.<br />She was supposed to stay there until she successfully escaped.<br />She thought everything would be back to normal.<br />But she was wrong.<br />She hasn’t been normal since.<br />Pierce and her mother moved to Isla Huesos where they thought they’d get a new start.<br />But the more Pierce tried to run away, the more she gets pulled towards the world that she has escaped.<br />The man that she was avoiding.<br />The man who she thinks she maybe falling in love with.<br /><br /><br />This book was definitely better than the other book I read.<br />I decided to read two myth-inspired books last week and was extremely disappointed with the other book. (Fury by Elizabeth Miles).<br />Anyways, what do I think about this book?<br />Definitely better than the other but not best, not outstanding, it was just okay.<br /><br />This is a YA-Paranormal Romance novel right? Because if it is, the romance part was kind of lacking for me.<br />It was good that Pierce and John were not all lovey-dovey because that was getting old.<br />But a little more spark between them would have been good.<br />It was lacking something.<br />Chemistry maybe?<br />Pierce was I dunno a little dull for me.<br />So was John.<br /><br />This would be my first Meg Cabot book.<br />It was good.<br />Not really really good that you’ll never forget this book.<br />It was a bit boring for most part.<br />A bit dragging.<br />There were loads of flashbacks but I thought the transitioning was good.<br />It wasn’t confusing which was good because most of this book was about the flashbacks.<br />Anyways, I am giving this book a 3.5.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9695741216572423999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1223675191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223675191" />
    <a title="Sophie Narey (Bookreview- aholic) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37868613-sophie-narey-bookreview--aholic"><img alt="Sophie Narey (Bookreview- aholic) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532961691p2/37868613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1223675191?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie Narey (Bookreview- aholic) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie Narey (Bookreview- aholic) " href="/user/show/37868613-sophie-narey-bookreview--aholic">Sophie Narey (Bookreview- aholic) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330453851" href="/book/show/11212855-abandon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223675191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4103772275911212565">Published: 1/09/2011 <br/>Author: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot' title='Meg Cabot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Meg Cabot</a><br/><br/>I first started reading this book as I loved Meg Cabot's other series ' The Mediator' and 'The Princess Diaries' , so I thought that I would try this series and see if she could write this genre just as brilliantly. <br/> This book features the character of Pierce and John, unfortunately I found it very hard to not compare the characters to Bella and Edward from Twilight as there are a lot of similarities. While reading this book it could have easily been any boo</span>
  <span id="freeText4103772275911212565" style="display:none">Published: 1/09/2011 <br />Author: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot" title="Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Meg Cabot</a><br /><br />I first started reading this book as I loved Meg Cabot's other series ' The Mediator' and 'The Princess Diaries' , so I thought that I would try this series and see if she could write this genre just as brilliantly. <br /> This book features the character of Pierce and John, unfortunately I found it very hard to not compare the characters to Bella and Edward from Twilight as there are a lot of similarities. While reading this book it could have easily been any book from the Twilight series. I was hoping that even with this being the same genre, that the author would be able to put her own unique twist on it. <br /> Even though I didn't enjoy reading this book and managed to finish it quickly but I couldn't help thinking that I would have preferred it to be a little more original.It also had a lot of spelling and grammar mistakes through out the novel which put me off and frustrated me a little bit. I definitely wouldn't say it is my favorite book that she has written, the story line doesn't really seem to go anywhere, I understand that authors sometimes do that so that you buy the next book, but there wasn't really a story line to follow on to the next book just continuous flashbacks to what has already happened, the characters don't really develop and just mainly about whether Pierce loves John or not. It gets quite tedious after awhile!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4103772275911212565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165741034?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/4404986-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4404986-maria?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165741034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7126109326578175510">I don't recommend <a href='http://bookchilla.wordpress.com/2011/06/20/book-review-abandon-by-meg-cabot/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Abandon</a>.<br/><br/>*****<br/><br/>What the F this book is supposed to be?!!<br/><br/>I was confused by Cabot’s writing style so it was hard to comprehend the story. The author writes like I already know about Pierce’s past when in fact, i don’t. Rewind, fast forward, double rewind – that’s i felt like when i was reading it.<br/><br/>Should Pierce come across as a resilient young woman or as a problem child who really doesn’t know what to do with her life? Her character was vague enough for me to not connect with her i</span>
  <span id="freeText7126109326578175510" style="display:none">I don't recommend <a href="http://bookchilla.wordpress.com/2011/06/20/book-review-abandon-by-meg-cabot/" rel="nofollow noopener">Abandon</a>.<br /><br />*****<br /><br />What the F this book is supposed to be?!!<br /><br />I was confused by Cabot’s writing style so it was hard to comprehend the story. The author writes like I already know about Pierce’s past when in fact, i don’t. Rewind, fast forward, double rewind – that’s i felt like when i was reading it.<br /><br />Should Pierce come across as a resilient young woman or as a problem child who really doesn’t know what to do with her life? Her character was vague enough for me to not connect with her in any way. John is not as engaging as i thought he would be. who the hell falls in love after meeting a 7-year-old girl then rages when that same girl died suddenly when she was fifteen? John is a stalker, that’s what he is. There is no way their love story is in that book – i know, i read and finished it!<br /><br />The conflict is nowhere near resolved. Just when i thought John and Pierce are going to take some action, i was already reading the acknowledgement page. *big sigh*<br /><br />I am definitely not reading another Meg Cabot book.</span>

<div id="review_1035186235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1035186235" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19598078-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568847131p2/19598078.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1035186235?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/19598078-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1035186235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3778303936229927595"><b>Possible spoilers below, proceed with caution</b><br/><br/>I honestly enjoyed this book up until the last 20% or so, though I found it odd and confusing the way the Author insisted on jumping from one thing to the next rapidly and without explanation or cause, for example: one minute the Main Character Pierce was talking to family or friends then suddenly she's thinking about something completely different and then we are thrown back in time to a memory that happened either when pierce was 7 or 15.. it was ha</span>
  <span id="freeText3778303936229927595" style="display:none"><b>Possible spoilers below, proceed with caution</b><br><br>I honestly enjoyed this book up until the last 20% or so, though I found it odd and confusing the way the Author insisted on jumping from one thing to the next rapidly and without explanation or cause, for example: one minute the Main Character Pierce was talking to family or friends then suddenly she's thinking about something completely different and then we are thrown back in time to a memory that happened either when pierce was 7 or 15.. it was hard to follow to put it nicely felt like we were going in circles, but still intriguing enough that I didn't want to put it down.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410129247ra/11065435.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I had a hard time rating this book because I really thought the story line had potential. It could have been 5 Star worthy but sadly it didn't live up to my expectations, especially towards the end when the insta-love started happening.<br><br><br>I finished Abandon at a family reunion, where I literally announced out loud " I think I'm going to be sick" and " I'm so glad this book ended because I was seriously contemplating beating my head against the table" but then I just told myself <b>"Better check yourself, before you wreck yourself"</b> just like Pierce did in the book like a FREAKING BAJILLION AND ONE TIMES!!! *SIGHS LOUDLY*.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410129247ra/11065436.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I also found it slightly sickening the fact that this girl fell in love with someone who had serious anger problem and pretty much kidnapped her. They spent more than half the book arguing or completely avoiding each other and the last bit making out when he wasn't kidnapping her, AGAIN!!!! Applause for Meg Cobat for setting a wonderful example for young girls about what a good healthy relationship looks like!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409717236ra/11012762.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Hey Pierce, here's something else for you to look up the meaning of "STOCKHOLM SYNDROME"!! If a guy falls in love with you when you are 7, and kidnaps you 2 times there is something wrong with his head.. and yours for loving him anyways after all that... JUST SAYING...<br> IM SO DONE!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404171487ra/10202102.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('T/mmM6c69/bPn9M+JszYKJJhGCsv/Ydun9xxWtl+d9l138/hHGQ+nmi0Z1/ROdL3RD7/4+FwCQnEojfrFD2FQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4bdJGsQV8/zzRyeAdfZytEQpMsDKQPS/BkXq1liOKRbbkSDIf0s6lFRsk+GCA3hrknbVCATNethdO6xnlc3bjA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13646658156664674211">Librarian note: AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll' title='Jenny Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot' title='Patricia Cabot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br/><br/>Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flun</span>
  <span id="freeText13646658156664674211" style="display:none">Librarian note: AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll" title="Jenny Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot" title="Patricia Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br /><br />Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flunked freshman Algebra twice, then decided to cut her own bangs. After six years as an undergrad at Indiana University, Meg moved to New York City (in the middle of a sanitation worker strike) to pursue a career as an illustrator, at which she failed miserably, forcing her to turn to her favorite hobby--writing novels--for emotional succor. She worked various jobs to pay the rent, including a decade-long stint as the assistant manager of a 700 bed freshmen dormitory at NYU, a position she still occasionally misses. <br /><br />She is now the author of nearly fifty books for both adults and teens, selling fifteen million copies worldwide, many of which have been #1 New York Times bestsellers, most notably The Princess Diaries series, which is currently being published in over 38 countries, and was made into two hit movies by Disney. In addition, Meg wrote the Mediator and 1-800-Where-R-You? series (on which the television series, Missing, was based), two All-American Girl books, Teen Idol, Avalon High, How to Be Popular, Pants on Fire, Jinx, a series of novels written entirely in email format (Boy Next Door, Boy Meets Girl, and Every Boy's Got One), a mystery series (Size 12 Is Not Fat/ Size 14 Is Not Fat Either/Big Boned), and a chick-lit series called Queen of Babble. <br /><br />Meg is now writing a new children's series called Allie Finkle's Rules for Girls. Her new paranormal series, Abandon, debuts in Summer of 2011. <br /><br />Meg currently divides her time between Key West, Indiana, and New York City with a primary cat (one-eyed Henrietta), various back-up cats, and her husband, who doesn't know he married a fire horse. Please don't tell him. <br /><br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45023-airhead" rel="nofollow noopener">Airhead</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43768-the-princess-diaries" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Diaries</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41667-mediator" rel="nofollow noopener">Mediator</a><br /></span>

  <!--
This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
